# Productivity

_156 messages · 21 participants · 2006-12 → 2007-01_

---

### Productivity

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2006-12-23T11:12:42+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4v33ipF1a006cU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
I've been doing a lot of thinking about productivity lately. (Of course 
thinking about something doesn't necessarily make you more productive, but 
you hope that it improves the quality of the end product.)

Just as an exercise and without any particular bias, I recently finished 
rewriting a COBOL application that originally took six weeks to develop. 
(This includes design, writing, testing/debugging). The design took around 4 
days, say, take a week off for design, and it took 5 weeks to develop.

It was rewritten in C# and DotNET in 5 days.

Given that I am a newbie in C#, but am no slouch when it comes to COBOL, I 
was at a loss to explain this.

1. Having developed it once, it is true that I now understand the whole 
thing a lot better.
2. Part of the 5 days for the C# development was spent doing video tutorials 
on C#.
3. Some of the things that took a fair bit of effort in OO COBOL were easy 
in DotNET.

But despite all of that, it is quite obvious that my productivity in Visual 
Studio 2005 is MUCH better than my productivity using the Fujitsu IDE.

This made me think about tools.

VS 2005 provides an Interactive Development Environment that is simply years 
ahead of any other development environment I have ever worked in (on both 
mainframes and PCs).

Colour coding of code, rollaway windows that you can pin down when you want 
them or send to a tab when you don't, intuitive context sensitive tooltips, 
having all your defined variables available for selection at the moment you 
want to reference them, having all methods, events and properties for the 
object you are referencing available as you type, along with help tooltips 
for any you select, ...all of these things collectively add up to MAJOR 
productivity improvements. There's no flipping through a listing (or opening 
other windows on the data division) to check variable names. No wondering or 
having to check parameter lists to methods. No syntax errors; you simply 
can't make them. No spelling errors...(Keywords are inserted for you and 
variables are selected from lists as you begin typing the name).  You can 
view or hide any section of code at any time. Online contextual help is 
instantly available for any method you want to use. If you don't know what 
methods are available (always part of the problem when you start learning 
something), they are organised by type so you can browse them instantly.

But.most importantly of all, the environment is NOT focused on code 
development. It is pure event driven programming. You DON'T start by writing 
IDENTIFICATION DIVISION (or its equivalent). You design what you want and 
the code for the events is placed into the right contexts for you. All of 
the housekeeping, fixed context, and overhead is hidden (unless you WANT to 
see it). You focus totally on your application and what you want to happen 
when events occur in it.

I find myself wondering how much quicker I could have built COBOL apps if I 
had had this kind of development environment.

I understand that Fujitsu DotNET COBOL comes with this environment. It costs 
several thousand dollars (if you can get them to sell it to you...I 
couldn't).

Visual C# Express comes with the same environment and is a FREE download. 
(This has been so for nearly two years now. I wouldn't be surprised if they 
stop it soon...) MicroSoft WANT you to use their products. They are 
confident (and with good reason) that, once you experience this environment, 
you will want to upgrade to Enterprise version and support multiple teams 
all working in it. (The enterprise version also supports source control).

There are over 400 FREE video tutorials on C# available on the web, 
thousands of code snippets and samples, and a positive and upbeat user 
community which is growing daily.

(What am I doing here... :-))

After a couple of months evaluating alternatives to COBOL, I am satisfied 
that C# and Java between them have everything I need. Visual Studio is 
simply the icing on the cake. I don't need to write off my existing 
investment in COBOL, as DotNET  runs my existing COBOL components as 
unmanaged code. (This will do until I need to replace them, if I need to 
replace them.) I have been finding ways to minimize COBOL maintenance for 
some years now, and components achieve this. I simply use C# as the glue to 
hold them together.

So, it looks like I will be winding down my COBOL development.

The tools for cutting edge development are MUCH better and cheaper than 
COBOL. It remains useful for batch development, which is what it was 
invented for, and where we came in...

Forty years of writing it.

Guess it's time for a change... :-)

Pete.
```

"HeyBub" <heybubNOSPAM@gmail.com> wrote in message 
news:12oosqtmgaqcd81@news.supernews.com...
> Pete Dashwood wrote:
>>
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> to do with program development - maybe more than anything else.

The same way luck decides who wins at Chess? :-)

I'm not dismissing luck; as a keen Backgammon player I know that a lucky 
player will beat an expert player, in the short term. In the long term; 
skill will out. And every lucky streak eventually goes cold...

Nevertheless, your comment may be fair, because I only have a sample of one 
and it COULD be luck.

I don't think it is. I don't think it is because, (when it comes to 
programming) I am meticulous and have acquired skill. Assigning success to 
having lucked out, simply devalues the many hours of thought and effort I 
invested in the project..


>
> How many times have you said to yourself: "I'll be damned. It worked the 
> first time!"

When this happens it isn't luck; it is care, thought, skill, and a lot of 
sweat. I EXPECT stuff to work the first time; If it takes more than 3 
compiles, I start thinking about a redesign...:-)

I should qualify this by saying that I write and debug at a function level. 
I don't write huge programs with thousands of lines of code and then compile 
them as a single entity.  I write say, 50 to 100 lines  (a SECTION) then 
check that it works. The end product could be many thousands of lines, but 
that will be many building blocks glued together, and each block will be 
separately focused on, designed, built and debugged. (And many of these are 
simply reusable modules that are plugged in and are known to work.) .

And how many times have you just never been able to get the
> sucker to function at all?

Only once. Forty years ago... the very first production program I ever wrote 
in COBOL. It had to produce 6 reports and one of them never worked... :-) 
These days if I found myself writing code that never worked, I'd consider 
some other form of employment...

>
> Same tools, experience, money, etc. The only difference is providence.

No, I've never been to Rhode Island so I don't know what life changing 
catharsis could be experienced there, and I don't believe in a Higher Power 
who throws dice to decide whether COBOL programs work or not. Providence 
simply doesn't cut it for me.

I am reasonably satisfied in this instance that, although luck cannot be 
ruled out, it is far more probable that the superiority of the tools made 
the difference.

I have come to believe in Visual Studio 2005... : -)  The DotNET framework 
also simplifies a number of  things.

(And C# is a pretty cool language too...)

It seems I am not the only one finding this. Demand for C# skills has almost 
doubled in the last 6 months and is still steeply rising.

Quote from 'Information Week'  October 4th, 2006...

"Hudson sees particularly strong demand for developers, especially those 
with C# skills, says Taylor. At this time last year, the demand from Hudson 
clients for developers was 70% related to Java, 25% to C#, and 5% to C++. 
That's not the case this year, with 70% of demand for developers with C# 
talent, 25% for Java, and 5% for C++. "

Here's the full article:

http://www.informationweek.com/management/showArticle.jhtml?articleID=193104411&subSection=Career+Development

People wondering where their COBOL career may be going, should consider 
this.

Sometimes it is comforting to have a parachute, even if the plane is flying 
steadily...

It isn't hard to learn but it DOES require some time and effort. And there 
are new concepts, (like OO), which reqire suspension of what you already 
know, and acceptance of a different way of approaching things.. There is a 
huge amount of information and (downloadable or runnable online video) 
tutorials available, at all levels of programming skill (including Absolute 
Beginner), for FREE, along with software and IDE downloads, for FREE. I have 
been quite stunned by the quality of some of this material and would expect 
to pay for it...


>
> Maybe you just got lucky.

Possible, but unlikely.

Pete.

> > Maybe you just got lucky.
>
> Possible, but unlikely.
>
> Pete.

I have no doubt you are very skilled, but a rewrite will take advantage
of a number of design decisions and perhaps experiments that may have
take the original writer some time to get right.  You also have to bear
in mind that perhaps you are more skilled than the person who
originally wrote it and would have done the job rather faster had you
written the original.  The difference can be dramatic and even the same
person could be a lot faster with regular practice or better training.

Perhaps a fairer comparison would be a two way test, where one person
rewrites a Java and C# application in OO COBOL of roughly similar
complexity.

Having said that, I am nevertheless very impressed and can see your
point.

Robert

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Productivity

_(reply depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2006-12-25T15:21:53+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4v8qu1F1b75r0U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4v33ipF1a006cU1@mid.individual.net> <12oosqtmgaqcd81@news.supernews.com> <4v7ajgF1bf6u8U1@mid.individual.net> <1166980834.471149.102990@i12g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`

```

"Robert Jones" <rjones0@hotmail.com> wrote in message 
news:1166980834.471149.102990@i12g2000cwa.googlegroups.com...
>
>> > Maybe you just got lucky.
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> take the original writer some time to get right.

I WAS the original designer/writer... that was the whole point. I was amazed 
because I expected the rewrite to take at least as long, given my 
inexperience with C#. And I noted in my post that  I had a better 
understanding the second time.

I am totally persuaded that the toolset makes a major difference.

The whole approach under VS 2005 allows you to focus entirely on the 
application and how you want it to behave. Hundreds (thousands?) of lines of 
working, debugged code are generated for you (in whatever language you have 
selected... C#, C++, or VB in the full version; I only have C# in the 
Express version) and you only NEED to write specific code for specific 
events. All of the necessary contexts are produced automatically as you 
specify event handling.

In the same way that we don't write COBOL programs from scratch, but take a 
previous program or template and modify it, VS2005 inserts what you actually 
write into the right place in the code and does all of the housekeeping and 
context for you. (You can change it if you want to, but so far I have not 
had any need to.) Things like allocation of namespaces, connection to 
appropriate support libraries, automatic scoping of variables and so on are 
all wrapped around your code and you never have to worry about them. It's 
like having someone present you with only the part of your COBOL template 
that you want to deal with right now, and then ensuring that any variables 
you create are automatically placed in the DATA division and any existing 
variables are available on a drop down that appears as soon as you reach a 
point where the syntax requires a dataname. (The list shrinks automatically 
as you type further characters, or you can simply select the dataname you 
want immediately from the list. There is no possibility of spelling or 
syntax errors, unless you force them deliberately... I did this just to see 
what compiler diagnostics looked like and how they were presented; if I 
hadn't, I never would have seen this... :-)) Not only that, but a tooltip 
describing the picture of the variable flashes up when you move the mouse 
over the list. No more keeping listings of the data division while you write 
procedure division code, or having to refer back to see what you named 
something...it is all automatically at your fingertips.

That is just one tiny part of it. It is a truly interactive environment and 
you interact with it to describe your application, rather than to write 
code. The whole thing is component based and appropriate components are 
simply dragged and dropped to where you want them. The DotNET framework is 
an "object rich" environment, so a very large percentage of what you want is 
already available. Things like list views, directory searches, etc are a 
mouse click to install then you can decide what properties you want set, and 
when.

I remember battling to get the standard directory/file selection dialog 
included in an OO COBOL  (PowerCOBOL)application. It was difficult and 
non-intuitive. There was no documentation provided by Fujitsu and I had no 
idea what the component was even called or where it lived. I had to use an 
Object Browser to locate it amongst thousands of Operating System 
components, and then try and figure out what its methods, properties, 
events, and interfaces were and provide the correct format for them in 
COBOL. Finally got it working, but it took a day. In C#/DotNET I did the 
same job in literally 5 minutes, dragging the component from the toolbar 
directly into my codeview. And it displays in the Windows XP theme 
automatically, so the program does not look "alien" to the user. I actually 
wrote 9 lines of code to support this, and 6 of those are comments...:

Here's the C# code:

private void button1_Click(object sender, EventArgs e)    //provided by 
VS2005
{ 
//provided by VS2005

/* User clicks "Browse for database" button. Open the standard dialog
* and put the selected file and path into the current form.
*
* This is only for MS ACCESS... other databases and ODBC have other 
selections.
*
*/

openFileDialog1.InitialDirectory = "C:\\";         // start at the 
beginning...
openFileDialog1.ShowDialog();
textBox1.Text = openFileDialog1.FileName;

} 
//provided by VS2005

(I have included the // strings for clarity. They don't appear in the actual 
listing.) The code to actually construct the "openFileDialog1" object is 
automatically included in the right place in the C# program as soon as I 
drag and drop the component icon from the DotNET toolbox. I never need to 
refer or even look at it, just use the object immediately. Furthermore, it 
has default properties that ensure that any selection made is a valid path 
and the file selected actually exists...

First time I've done it in this environment... 5 minutes work.(Drag and drop 
took seconds...) Tested it, worked perfectly first time (Jerry, please note 
:-))

Here's the same stuff in OO COBOL... (about 10 hours work the first time I 
wrote it, at least 1 hour to debug)...

 ENVIRONMENT     DIVISION.
 DATA            DIVISION.
 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
 01 FileMask Pic X(55) Value "ACCESS RDB Files (.mdb .mde)|*.mdb;*.mde|All 
Files|*.*".
 01 DeskFile.
    12 FileName Pic X(255) Value Spaces.
    12 Filler Pic X Value X"00".
 01  ReturnValue pic s9(4) comp-5.
 PROCEDURE       DIVISION.
 a000.
     Move Spaces to FileName
     INVOKE POW-SELF "GetFileName" USING FileName
            "Select ACCESS Database File"
            FileMask
            POW-CDOPEN
            RETURNING ReturnValue
     END-INVOKE

* If ReturnValue is true, user did select a db...
     if ReturnValue = POW-TRUE
        move FileName to DB-path
     else
       move spaces to DB-path
     end-if
     move DB-path to "Text" of CmText2
     if DB-path NOT = spaces
        move spaces to "Text" of CmText1
        call 'SetCaption'
     else
        invoke CmText2 "SetFocus"
     end-if
     .
 a999.
     exit.

(Note that I wrote 33 lines for this solution

There are a number of other code snippets associated with the above, to do 
things like path and file validation etc., which I haven't shown here. 
(these are not required in the C# solution because the DotNET component 
validates whatever is returned, automatically, unless you tell it not to...)

You can see that the component used in the COBOL solution requires 
parameters, whereas the one used in the DotNET solution does not, using 
properties instead. (I much prefer this, as discussed here previously.)

The COBOL event processing requires a complete COBOL nested program with all 
the ENVIRONMENT, DATA, and PROCEDURE Division headers and you must write 
these yourself. (PowerCOBOL will generate the headers only, but NetCOBOL 
does not.)

The VS2005 solution automatically generates the correct context instantly, 
and opens in code view with the cursor between the braces ready for you to 
write your code. The full toolbox of components is available to you and in 
many cases you don't need to do anything, other than invoke the main method 
of whatever component you want activated, or cut and paste a code snippet 
from the thousands that are available.

The VS2005 solution is completely Object Oriented with the focus being on 
Objects (represented by icons that can be dragged and dropped from the 
toolbox) that can help you implement your application, rather than the focus 
being entirely on code and writing or copying it to build a solution.

Working with objects forces you to visualize your solution as a series of 
components, like machines on a production line. This is more productive for 
me than focusing on sections of code, which tends to lead to "thinking in 
code" for solutions. The code that MUST be written is presented without all 
the housekeeping and initializing that must be done in a code oriented 
approach, and the VS2005 IDE provides support for writing code which is 
light years ahead of simple Editors.

It is a different (and, in my opinion, hugely better) way to approach 
solution provision.

> You also have to bear
> in mind that perhaps you are more skilled than the person who
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> complexity.

That would be like rewriting COBOL back into Assembler. Pretty pointless.

>
> Having said that, I am nevertheless very impressed and can see your
> point.

Thank you, Robert. I'm not on commission here, just passing on experience in 
the hope that it may be of use to somebody. Positive feedback in this forum 
is, sadly, a rarity, but I've become used to that... :-)

Some of what I'm saying is unpalatable to people here, but that has never 
stopped me in the past. I suggested people start expanding their skill sets 
over 10 years ago (HERESY: COBOL is the only righteous and just way to 
implement computer applications. "Everything I need to do, I can do in 
COBOL...") and stop betting their futures on a one trick pony. Some took 
that advice and are happily employed today, others didn't and are sweating 
it...and some didn't and are quite happy as they see retirement coming up 
anyway. :-)

I'm NOT anti-COBOL. It fed and clothed me for decades and I'm not so 
churlish as to bite the hand that did that. Besides, like most people who 
have become proficient in this years-ahead-of-its-time, imaginative and 
innovative approach to commercial programming, I love writing it :-).

I am genuinely sorry to see it go, but I think it should be allowed to die 
with dignity, rather than having more and more things  "bolted on" to it in 
a futile attempt to bring it "up-to-date" or to compete with C++ or 
whatever. With the possible exception of adding OO to it, which was a simply 
stunning feat of software engineering that never caught the imagination of 
the user community (some would say they are a notoriously unimaginative 
lot...:-)), the fuctionality already embodied in it should be more than 
enough to meet the requirements where COBOL is the best choice of tool 
(Primarily, commercial batch processing...) Instead, we see resources being 
applied to adding XML to it... It's like trying to put out a fire by 
throwing gasoline on it. By the time this facility becomes available, if it 
ever does, the people who actually needed it will have moved to third party 
components and will be phasing out COBOL anyway.

We need to be realistic, not bury our heads in the sand, and realise there 
are events happening in the World at large that have a big impact on whether 
COBOL will continue to be used or not.

I gave it until 2015 (in 1996), before I believed it could be considered a 
"dead" language. I stand by that. But it's only 8 years away and a young 
programmer with a wife/husband and a mortgage needs to ensure his/her 
future. The answer is to use the right tools for the job and to see that 
your toolbox contains as many of these tools as possible. Whether we like it 
or not, alternatives to COBOL need to be looked at.

By "tools", I'm not just talking about languages and packages, but also 
approaches, methodologies, and better and more productive ways to do things.

Component based solutions are empowering us to do that. (I won't say "I told 
you so"... but, I did ... :-))

Pete.
```

still not free and not for 'production use'.  Now I'm not being a Micro
Focus apologist here.  I totally agree that they care little to nothing
about the little guy.  I was just pointing out that it is, and I think
you'll agree, Visual Studio itself that makes this so easy, and not any
particular language.  I have nothing against C#, and for Windows development
I think I'd probably agree that it's a much better answer than any form of
COBOL.

>How does openFileDialog1 get instantiated?

Umm, how does it in your example?  I only posted the COBOL corresponding to
your C# example.

Anyway, the instantiation of openFileDialog1 is generated by VS, just like
I'm sure it was in your example.  I can't remember exactly (I only have it
at home), but I believe it was something like...

   set openFileDialog1 = System-Windows-Forms-OpenFileDialog::"NEW"()

>How do you know what library is required?

I have no idea.  

>What happens if no file is selected?

Dunno, but I believe that's a function of the .NET runtime.  I will try it
and see what happens.

>Suppose the selected file is deleted moments after you select it?

I am no where near proficient in WinForms or any kind of event driven
program.  The fact that I could even come up with the code above is only
thanks to the ease of use of VS2005!

>I'm also still waiting for your comments on the nested perform I posted 
>sample code for, in response to your comment about that...
>
>Am I wasting my time here? :-)

Umm, maybe.  I didn't know I was supposed to respond.  I was only commenting

```

"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in message 
news:4vfl66F1as7a4U1@mid.individual.net...
> Pete Dashwood<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> 12/27/06 3:40 AM >>>
>>What happens if no file is selected?
>
> Dunno, but I believe that's a function of the .NET runtime.  I will try it
> and see what happens.

    Perhaps the string will be set to null or the empty string or something 
similar. It's probably explicitly stated in the OpenFileDialog 
documentation.

>
>>Suppose the selected file is deleted moments after you select it?
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> thanks to the ease of use of VS2005!

    Nothing will happen yet... the only thing your code does is to get a 
string representing the path to the selected file (before it was deleted). 
Now, if all you're going to do is display that string to user, no problem 
should arise (except maybe for a confused user who can no longer find 
specified file). But if you try to open that file, then a 
FileNotFoundException will probably get thrown.

    In Java, the compiler would complain unless you explicitly put code to 
deal with the possibility of that exception arising. In .NET, the compiler 
wouldn't say anything, and if the exception DOES come up during runtime, and 
you haven't added code to handle it, the program will just terminate, 
possibly emitting some debugging info (e.g. a stack trace) to the console.

    - Oliver
```

I was only joking about that.  If I ever came upon a situation where it
appears this construct would be useful I would have no problem using it.  I
just don't recall ever coming upon such a thing.  Or, if I did, I probably
didn't realize it and thus did something else.  :-)

I am certainly *not* against using all of the power that COBOL provides.  I
only recently used DECLARATIVES recently to handle file I/O errors.  It's
actually quite nice, not having to check the status after each I/O.  Should
be a bit more powerful to be *really* useful, but I'd be happy to see others
understand and use it.  My manager at first was against my use of this, but
I convinced him by pointing out that it's an "implicit perform" rather than
an "implicit goto".

I've also recently been using UNSTRING, which I hadn't made a lot of use of
in the past.  Below is something I was working on the other day.  I had
hoped to be able to get it in to a single "UNSTRING", but I ended up with
two and I'm fairly happy with it.  Essentially, it parses some input where
fields are delimited by '�' (MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER), and for each field there
can be both a parm name and a parm value delimited by '='
(MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR), or just a parm name (no '=').  Each perform of
300-PARSE-INPUT-DATA should result in the parsing of one field, putting the
parm name into INPUT-STRING-ID and the parm value (if present) into
INPUT-STRING-PARM.  If the field is a "null" field (essentially '��') then
the flag END-OF-REQUEST should be set.

 300-PARSE-INPUT-DATA.                                
     MOVE LOW-VALUES TO INPUT-STRING-ID               
                        INPUT-STRING-PARM             
                        STRING-ID-DELIM               
                        STRING-PARM-DELIM             
     MOVE ZEROES TO STRING-ID-LEN                     
                    STRING-PARM-LEN                   
     IF INPUT-DATA-POS > INPUT-DATA-LENGTH            
        SET END-OF-REQUESTS TO TRUE                   
     ELSE                                             
        UNSTRING INPUT-DATA                           
                 DELIMITED BY MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER     
                           OR MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR     
        INTO INPUT-STRING-ID                          
             DELIMITER IN STRING-ID-DELIM             
             COUNT IN STRING-ID-LEN                   
        POINTER INPUT-DATA-POS                        
        END-UNSTRING                                  
        IF STRING-ID-DELIM = MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR      
            UNSTRING INPUT-DATA                       
                     DELIMITED BY MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER 
            INTO INPUT-STRING-PARM                    
                 DELIMITER IN STRING-PARM-DELIM       
                 COUNT IN STRING-PARM-LEN          
            POINTER INPUT-DATA-POS                 
            END-UNSTRING                           
        END-IF                                     
        IF STRING-ID-LEN = ZERO                    
           SET END-OF-REQUEST TO TRUE              
        END-IF                                     

I'm guessing there is no way to make this a single UNSTRING, but if anyone
can do it I'd love to see it!  :-)

>Of course you are not required to respond; I just hoped that you would. (My

>post was in response to yours).

Sorry.  I simply didn't feel I had any more to add.

INPUT-STRING-ID=userId
INPUT-STRING-PARM=FJS

INPUT-STRING-ID=location
INPUT-STRING-PARM=AURO

INPUT-STRING-ID=function
INPUT-STRING-PARM=filmRequest

300-PARSE-INPUT-DATA is done there's a validation routine, and if the parm
is valid then INPUT-STRING-ID and INPUT-STRING-PARM are placed into just
such an array.  That array is then passed to the appropriate sub-program
(depending on the value of the "function" parameter) for further
processing.

```

"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message 
news:4vlnqgF1c247oU1@mid.individual.net...
>
OK, as promised here is a complete working program.

I really enjoyed doing this :-)

The hard parts were confining myself to the B margin and using upper case...

Fortunately the sun has come out and I'm off to a cocktail party so it might 
not be perfect. I ran it and checked the output; (the ARGUMENTS array)... it 
looked good.

You may need to remove all the *> comments if your compiler doesn't support 
them; the rest should compile OK.

Should be able to cut and paste the code below directly into your editor. It 
should run as written.

 IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
 PROGRAM-ID.     NVPARMS.
 AUTHOR.         PETER E. C. DASHWOOD.
 DATE-WRITTEN.   DECEMBER 30TH, 2006.
*REMARKS.
*
*  A SET OF "PARAMETERS" MUST BE PARSED AND PRESENTED TO A
*  PROGRAM
*  FOR PROCESSING
*
*  IN FACT, THESE ARE NOT "PARAMETERS" AT ALL BUT ARE REALLY
*  AN INPUT
*  FILE...
*
*  NEVERTHELESS THE PROGRAM DEMONSTRATES SOME USES OF:
*     UNSTRING
*     COMPLEX PERFORM
*     INSPECT
*
*  THE COMPLETE PARAMETER SET IS STORED TO AN ARRAY DURING
*  INITIALIZATION AS A 'ONE-TIME' TASK.
*
*  THIS ARRAY COULD BE VALIDATED DURING INITIALIZATION ALSO,
*  AND ENTRIES IN IT CROSS-REFERENCED IF REQUIRED.
*
*  BY ISOLATING THE CODE TO LOAD THE ARGUMENTS INTO THE
*  INITIALIZATION
*  PART OF THE PROGRAM, THIS CODE COULD BE USED IN ANY PROGRAM
*  THAT HAD A SIMILAR PARAMETER FORMAT. DOING IT FROM THE
*  MAINLINE ON A PARAMETER BY PARAMETER BASIS PREVENTS THIS.
*

 ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
 CONFIGURATION SECTION.
 SOURCE-COMPUTER. IBM-PC.
 OBJECT-COMPUTER. IBM-PC.
 DATA DIVISION.
 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
 01  ARGUMENTS.
     12 NAME-VALUE-PAIR OCCURS 40
                        INDEXED BY ARGS-X1.
        15 ARG-NAME    PIC X(25).
        15 ARG-VALUE   PIC X(25).
        15 ARG-EOG     PIC X.  *> INDICATES THAT THIS ENTRY IS
                               *> THE END OF A "GROUP" OF
                               *> PARAMETERS.

           88 ARG-END-OF-GROUP  VALUE '1'.

 01  ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT   PIC S9(4) COMP VALUE 40.
*> MUST MATCH VALUE IN OCCURS ABOVE.

 01  IN-DATA.
     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
     "userId=FJS�location=AURO�function=filmRequest�acct".
     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
     "Number=1234567890�userExtension=1403�routing=branc".
     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
     "h�routeLoc=K-MISS�routeAttn=Joe�comments=Comments ".
     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
     "Go Here�debit�date=121306�amount=100.00�sequenceNb".
     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
     "r=12345678��credit�date=051406�amount=900.00�seque".
     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
     "nceNbr=11122233��ATM�date=010106�amount=123.45��ch".
     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
     "argeback�date=010106�amount=500.00��statement�date".
     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
     "=032906�amount=1000.00�                           ".
 01  INPUT-DATA REDEFINES IN-DATA PIC X(400).


 01  VARIOUS-COUNTS USAGE COMP.
     12 MAX-ARGUMENTS    PIC S9(4).
     12 INPUT-DATA-POS   PIC S9(4).
     12 STRING-PARM-LEN  PIC S9(4).
     12 MYTALLY1         PIC S9(4).
     12 MYTALLY2         PIC S9(4).
     12 INPUT-DATA-LENGTH PIC S9(4).
     12 NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS PIC S9(4).


 01  VARIOUS-OTHER-DATA.
     12 INPUT-STRING-ID     PIC X(25).
     12 INPUT-STRING-PARM   PIC X(25).
     12 NV-WORK             PIC X(60).
     12 MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER PIC X VALUE "�".
     12 MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR PIC X VALUE "=".

 01  FLAGS.
     12 FINISH-FLAG         PIC X VALUE SPACE.
        88 FINISHED           VALUE '1'.
        88 NOT-FINISHED       VALUE '0'.
     12 REQUEST-FLAG        PIC X VALUE SPACE.
        88 END-OF-REQUEST           VALUE '1'.
        88 NOT-END-OF-REQUEST       VALUE '0'.



 PROCEDURE DIVISION.
 MAIN SECTION.
 000.
     PERFORM 100-INITIAL-SETUP
     PERFORM 200-PROCESSING UNTIL FINISHED
*     PERFORM 900-CLOSE-DOWN
     STOP RUN
     .
*>===========================================================
 100-INITIAL-SETUP SECTION.
 110-IS.
     SET NOT-FINISHED TO TRUE
     PERFORM 2000-LOAD-ARGUMENTS
      *> IN THIS SCENARIO THE ARGUMENTS ARE PARSED AND LOADED
      *> ONCE
      *> DURING INITIALIZATION.
      *>
      *> IT IS A GENERAL PURPOSE LOAD ROUTINE. (WORKS FOR ANY
      *> PROGRAM WITH PARAMETERS IN THE NAME=VALUE FORMAT).
      *>
      *>
      *> ON COMPLETION ALL ARGUMENTS HAVE BEEN LOADED INTO THE
      *> "ARGUMENTS" ARRAY. GROUPS OF ARGUMENTS THAT REPRESENT
      *> A "RECORD" WILL HAVE THE GROUP FLAG SET IN THE LAST NAME
      *> /VALUE PAIR OF THE GROUP
      *>
      *> INPUT-STRING-ID AND INPUT-STRING-PARM CAN BE LOADED FROM
      *> THIS
      *> ARRAY USING THE ARGS-X1 INDEX. THIS IS DONE BY PERFORMING
      *> 2100-PARSE-INPUT-DATA.
      *>
     .
 199-IS.
     EXIT.
*>================================================================

 200-PROCESSING SECTION.
 210-P.
     *> VARIOUS PROCESSING OCCURS HERE...

     PERFORM 2100-PARSE-INPUT-DATA  *> GET THE NEXT NAME/VALUE
                                    *> PAIR

     *> PROCESSING CONTINUES....USING INPUT-STRING-ID
     *>                           AND INPUT-STRING-PARM
     *> AS AT PRESENT.

     SET FINISHED TO TRUE
     .
 299-P.
     EXIT.
*>==============================================================
*>
*>          SUBROUTINES ACTIVATED FROM ABOVE...
*>
*>==============================================================
 2000-LOAD-ARGUMENTS     SECTION.
 2000-LA-000.
     *> THE FOLLOWING CODE PARSES THE NAME/VALUE PAIRS IN
     *> INPUT-DATA
     *> AND LOADS THEM INTO THE ARGUMENTS ARRAY.
     *>
     MOVE SPACES TO ARGUMENTS
     IF INPUT-DATA (1:1) = MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
        MOVE 2 TO INPUT-DATA-POS   *> STEP OVER FIRST FIELD
                                   *> DELIMITER
                                   *> IF ONE IS PRESENT
     ELSE
        MOVE 1 TO INPUT-DATA-POS
     END-IF
     COMPUTE INPUT-DATA-LENGTH = FUNCTION STORED-CHAR-LENGTH
                                          (INPUT-DATA)
     *> IF YOUR ENVIRONMENT DOESN'T SUPPORT THE ABOVE
     *> INTRINSIC FUNCTION, YOU WILL NEED TO ESTABLISH
     *> THE TOTAL LENGTH OF THE PARAMETER STRINGS
     *> IN "INPUT-DATA" USING "INSPECT" OR ONE OF THE
     *> TECHNIQUES DISCUSSED IN CLC
     MOVE ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT TO MAX-ARGUMENTS
     PERFORM
        VARYING ARGS-X1
           FROM 1
             BY 1
        UNTIL ARGS-X1 > MAX-ARGUMENTS OR
              INPUT-DATA-POS > INPUT-DATA-LENGTH
           MOVE SPACES TO NV-WORK
           UNSTRING
              INPUT-DATA
                 DELIMITED BY MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
                    INTO NV-WORK
                 COUNT IN STRING-PARM-LEN
                 WITH POINTER INPUT-DATA-POS
           END-UNSTRING
           IF INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) =
              MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
              SET ARG-END-OF-GROUP (ARGS-X1) TO TRUE
              ADD 1 TO INPUT-DATA-POS
           END-IF
           MOVE ZERO TO MYTALLY1
           INSPECT NV-WORK
              TALLYING MYTALLY1 FOR CHARACTERS
                   BEFORE MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR
           IF MYTALLY1 = STRING-PARM-LEN
              MOVE NV-WORK (1: MYTALLY1)
                TO ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1)
              MOVE SPACES TO ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1)
           ELSE
              MOVE NV-WORK (1: MYTALLY1)
                   TO ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1)
                 MOVE NV-WORK (MYTALLY1 + 2: STRING-PARM-LEN
                      - MYTALLY1 + 1)
                   TO ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1)
           END-IF
     END-PERFORM
     SET NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS TO ARGS-X1
     SUBTRACT 1 FROM NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS
     SET ARGS-X1 TO 1 *> SET INDEX FOR USE FROM MAINLINE CODE
     SET ARGS-X1 DOWN BY 1
     .
 2000-LA-999.
     EXIT.
 *>==============================================================
 2100-PARSE-INPUT-DATA     SECTION.
 2100-PID-000.
 *> THIS CODE LOADS INPUT-STRING-ID AND INPUT-STRING-PARM WITH
 *> THE NEXT
 *> VALID NAME/VALUE PAIR.
 *> IT DOESN'T PARSE THE INPUT-DATA BUT THE EFFECT IS THE SAME AS
 *> IF IT HAD...
     SET ARGS-X1 UP BY 1
     IF  ARGS-X1 NOT > NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS
         MOVE ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1) TO INPUT-STRING-ID
         MOVE ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1) TO INPUT-STRING-PARM
         IF ARG-END-OF-GROUP (ARGS-X1)
            SET END-OF-REQUEST TO TRUE
         ELSE
            SET NOT-END-OF-REQUEST TO TRUE
         END-IF
     ELSE
       MOVE SPACE TO INPUT-STRING-ID
                     INPUT-STRING-PARM
     END-IF
     .
 2100-PID-999.
     EXIT.
*>============================ END OF PROGRAM ===================

Cheers,

Pete.
```

```

"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message
news:4vm6ldF16ggd7U1@mid.individual.net...
[snip]
>  01  IN-DATA.
>      12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
>  01  INPUT-DATA REDEFINES IN-DATA PIC X(400).

Just an observation; but it seems easier to me,
when populating a large data item, to use the
STRING statement. For example, ...

move spaces to input-data
string
      "userId=FJS�location=AURO�function=filmRequest�acct"
      "Number=1234567890�userExtension=1403�routing=branc"
      "h�routeLoc=K-MISS�routeAttn=Joe�comments=Comments "
      "Go Here�debit�date=121306�amount=100.00�sequenceNb"
      "r=12345678��credit�date=051406�amount=900.00�seque"
      "nceNbr=11122233��ATM�date=010106�amount=123.45��ch"
      "argeback�date=010106�amount=500.00��statement�date"
      "=032906�amount=1000.00�"
delimited by size
into input-data.

And, multiple STRING statements allow
for multiple tests.

Furthermore, binary values may be inserted
by using hex literals (non-ANS 85). For example, ...

move spaces to cr-lf-separated-data
string
        "abc" x"0d0a" "def" x"0d0a" "ghi" x"0d0a"
delimited by size
into cr-lf-separated-data.

All this with no messy counting!
```

"Rick Smith" <ricksmith@mfi.net> wrote in message 
news:12pdftt926l3sb9@corp.supernews.com...
>
> "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message
…[51 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Yes, that's a good point.

Over the years (starting from before STRING was available) I tried many ways 
to insert long strings into COBOL programs. I'm sure most COBOL programmers 
have encountered the same problem. Continuation is ugly and not simple; most 
other definitions require counting as you point out, and that is also messy 
and error prone.

I tried concatenation (similar to what you would do in VB) and that worked 
OK but left me vaguely dissatisfied :-).

The above is as easy as I could make it on myself inasmuch as it is clear 
and you don't need to count. (Just take X columns from wherever you start... 
if it starts in 13 and you have defined X to be 50, it must end in 62, start 
+ X - 1).

The Fujitsu IDE I use to write COBOL shows line and column for wherever you 
put the cursor, so this is pretty simple. After doing the first one and 
checking it, it is a simple matter to copy this and insert the rest.

Your point about hex literals is well taken, and for this it would certainly 
be necessary to either concatenate or use STRING.

Pete.
```

```
"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message 
news:4vo2ueF1cg635U1@mid.individual.net...

> "Rick Smith" <ricksmith@mfi.net> wrote in message 
> news:12pdftt926l3sb9@corp.supernews.com...
<snip>

> Over the years (starting from before STRING was available) I tried many ways 
> to insert long strings into COBOL programs. I'm sure most COBOL programmers 
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Whatever one may (or may not) think about the '02 ISO COBOL Standard, I *REALLY* 
like the fix for continuing alphanumeric literals, i.e.

   "ABC"-
   "defg  "-
   "x"

Allows you to NOT count where the "R-margin" or the continuation column or 
trailing blanks are.

It is worth nothing this is QUITE different from the (X/Open and some compilers 
as an extension)

   "ABC" &
   "defg  " &
   "x"

which is treated as one alphanumeric literal at "run-time" but as 3 separate 
text words for COPY/REPLACING and REPLACE.
```

"William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com> wrote in message
news:nR%lh.234771$7G.106201@fe08.news.easynews.com...
[snip]
>
> Whatever one may (or may not) think about the '02 ISO COBOL Standard, I
*REALLY*
> like the fix for continuing alphanumeric literals, i.e.
>
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…

compilers
> as an extension)

…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> which is treated as one alphanumeric literal at "run-time" but as 3
separate
> text words for COPY/REPLACING and REPLACE.

The above seems to suggest that concatenation
is not available in ISO/IEC 1989:2002 COBOL.
See page 118, 8.7.3 Concatenation operator,
"The concatenation operator is the COBOL
character '&', which shall be immediately
preceded and followed by a separator space."

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Concatenation in COBOL (was Re: Continuation in COBOL)

_(reply depth: 18)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2007-01-01T21:27:04+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<H0fmh.231422$6O4.162918@fe09.news.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<4v33ipF1a006cU1@mid.individual.net> <12oosqtmgaqcd81@news.supernews.com> <4v7ajgF1bf6u8U1@mid.individual.net> <1166980834.471149.102990@i12g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <4v8qu1F1b75r0U1@mid.individual.net> <dElkh.4094$yx6.3439@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net> <4vf0t1F1bfj5nU1@mid.individual.net> <4vfl66F1as7a4U1@mid.individual.net> <4vgj6mF1a4g7nU1@mid.individual.net> <4vimr5F1cedo7U1@mid.individual.net> <4vj2kkF1co1akU1@mid.individual.net> <4vlbkiF1bf56sU1@mid.individual.net> <4vlnqgF1c247oU1@mid.individual.net> <4vm6ldF16ggd7U1@mid.individual.net> <12pdftt926l3sb9@corp.supernews.com> <4vo2ueF1cg635U1@mid.individual.net> <nR%lh.234771$7G.106201@fe08.news.easynews.com> <12pi7257hchfb4c@corp.supernews.com>`

```
Sorry if I was unclear. I meant to say that many implementors provided "&" 
concatenation as an extension to the '85 Standard - as this was what X/Open 
specified (and it was an '85 Standard based specification).  It is absolutely 
true that it is part of the '02 Standard (and that is where the new format 
continuation came in BECAUSE concatenation uses separate text words)
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Productivity

_(reply depth: 15)_

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>
- **Date:** 2007-01-02T10:31:10-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

>
>
…[42 more quoted lines elided]…
>for multiple tests.

Another nice thing about this is that you can use the POINTER clause to set
the length, eg...

move 1 to input-ptr
string 'stuff goes here. '
       'more stuff here. '
       'even more stuff.'
  delimited by size
  into input-data
  with pointer input-ptr
subtract 1 from input-ptr giving input-data-length

Pretty cool.

Frank

Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA

```
Frank Swarbrick wrote:
> Another nice thing about this is that you can use the POINTER clause to set
> the length, eg...
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> Pretty cool.

Very cool.  We use it when we're building XML extract files for 
interfaces (which, since it's the mandated "thou shalt" format, we're 
doing more and more).  It keeps us from having to use fixed-length 
records (although some of the lazier guys have still been doing that... 
grrr.....).

Anyway, I usually do something like this - say the data we're supposed 
to send is tagged with "SerialNumber".

-8<-

move 1 to wsPtr
string "<SerialNumber" delimited by size
   into wsBuildArea
     with pointer wsPtr
end-string

if wsSerialNumber = spaces
     string " />" delimited by size
       into wsBuildArea
         with pointer wsPtr
     end-string
else
     string ">"  wsSerialNumber  "</SerialNumber>" delimited by space
       into wsBuildArea
         with pointer wsPtr
     end-string
end-if

->8-

At this point, wsPtr now has the length of the build area, which can be 
used to write a variable-length record, or used to string piece-meal 
into an output accrual area.

And to think, when STRING was developed, XML didn't even exist!  :) 
There are several things in COBOL that are like this too - they didn't 
exist, but the facilities that exist are great for it.
```

Code deleted

I had to make one minor change to make this work:

INSPECT NV-WORK
   TALLYING MYTALLY1 FOR CHARACTERS
        BEFORE MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR 

has to be changed to

INSPECT NV-WORK (1:STRING-PARM-LEN)
   TALLYING MYTALLY1 FOR CHARACTERS
        BEFORE MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR 

Or you could probably keep the original inspect and change the IF statement
from
IF MYTALLY1 = STRING-PARM-LEN

to

IF MYTALLY1 = FUNCTION LENGTH(NV-WORK)

Though I didn't try that one out.  I prefer the former.

In any case, and don't take this the wrong way, your result isn't actually
what I was looking for.  What I wanted, and pretty much knew was not
possible, was to get the two fields INPUT-STRING-ID and INPUT-STRING-PARM
set based solely on a single UNSTRING.  No temporary fields (NV-WORK)
allowed.  Of course I did not state that explicitly, so you couldn't have
been expected to know.

I actually originally had something similar to what you had.  I used a
second UNSTRING instead of the INSPECT followed by MOVE.  Reworking your
example, it might have looked something like this...

     PERFORM                                        
        VARYING ARGS-X1                             
           FROM 1                                   
             BY 1                                   
        UNTIL ARGS-X1 > MAX-ARGUMENTS OR            
              INPUT-DATA-POS > INPUT-DATA-LENGTH    
           MOVE SPACES TO NV-WORK                   
           UNSTRING                                 
              INPUT-DATA                            
                 DELIMITED BY MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER   
                    INTO NV-WORK                    
                 COUNT IN STRING-PARM-LEN           
                 WITH POINTER INPUT-DATA-POS        
           END-UNSTRING                             
           IF STRING-PARM-LEN = ZERO                
              SET ARG-END-OF-GROUP (ARGS-X1) TO TRUE
           ELSE                                     
              UNSTRING                              
                 NV-WORK (1:STRING-PARM-LEN)        
                    DELIMITED BY MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR
                       INTO ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1)      
                            ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1)     
              END-UNSTRING                          
           END-IF
     END-PERFORM 

(Everything before and after this loop is unchanged.)

The thing I like about my original method, other than requiring two
unstrings, is that no temporary field is required.

Anyway, thanks for giving it a shot!

Frank

:-) I guessed as much but I took you at your word... :-)

This whole (thoroughly enjoyable) exercise made me think about a few 
things...

I mentioned somewhere else recently that when we are dealing with code based 
solutions we tend to think in terms of a code based solution.

In this case you were thinking about using UNSTRING and looking for a 
solution that incorporates that.

(There's nothing wrong with that and it's how we all learn to use code and 
get experience in writing it.)

Sometimes though it can blind us to the essentials of the solution.

If I had really been faced with this problem, my solution would not have 
used UNSTRING (ANY number of them), work fields, or anything else that is 
really extraneous and/or unnecessary.

Here's the solution I actually would have written...(I have included the 
whole thing so it can be easily pasted into an editor and 
compiled/debugged... you and I may not be the only ones following this... 
:-))

000010 IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
000011 PROGRAM-ID.     NVPARMS.
000013 AUTHOR.         PETER E. C. DASHWOOD.
000014 DATE-WRITTEN.   DECEMBER 30TH, 2006.
000015*REMARKS.
000016*
000017*  A SET OF "PARAMETERS" MUST BE PARSED AND PRESENTED TO A
000018*  PROGRAM
000019*  FOR PROCESSING
000020*
000021*  IN FACT, THESE ARE NOT "PARAMETERS" AT ALL BUT ARE REALLY
000022*  AN INPUT
000023*  FILE...
000024*
000025*  NEVERTHELESS THE PROGRAM DEMONSTRATES SOME USES OF:
000026*     UNSTRING
000027*     COMPLEX PERFORM
000028*     COMPLEX INSPECT
000029*
000030*  THE COMPLETE PARAMETER SET IS STORED TO AN ARRAY DURING
000031*  INITIALIZATION AS A 'ONE-TIME' TASK.
000032*
000033*  THIS ARRAY COULD BE VALIDATED DURING INITIALIZATION ALSO,
000034*  AND ENTRIES IN IT CROSS-REFERENCED IF REQUIRED.
000035*
000036*  BY ISOLATING THE CODE TO LOAD THE ARGUMENTS INTO THE
000037*  INITIALIZATION
000038*  PART OF THE PROGRAM, THIS CODE COULD BE USED IN ANY PROGRAM
000039*  THAT HAD A SIMILAR PARAMETER FORMAT. DOING IT FROM THE
000040*  MAINLINE ON A PARAMETER BY PARAMETER BASIS PREVENTS THIS.
000041*
000042
000043 ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
000044 CONFIGURATION SECTION.
000045 SOURCE-COMPUTER. IBM-PC.
000046 OBJECT-COMPUTER. IBM-PC.
000056 DATA DIVISION.
000057 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
000058 01  ARGUMENTS.
000059     12 NAME-VALUE-PAIR OCCURS 40
000060                        INDEXED BY ARGS-X1.
000061        15 ARG-NAME    PIC X(25).
000062        15 ARG-VALUE   PIC X(25).
000063        15 ARG-EOG     PIC X.  *> INDICATES THAT THIS ENTRY IS
000064                               *> THE END OF A "GROUP" OF
000065                               *> PARAMETERS.
000066
000067           88 ARG-END-OF-GROUP  VALUE '1'.
000068
000069 01  ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT   PIC S9(4) COMP VALUE 40.
000070*> MUST MATCH VALUE IN OCCURS ABOVE.
000072
000080 01  IN-DATA.
000081     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000083     "userId=FJS�location=AURO�function=filmRequest�acct".
000084     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000086     "Number=1234567890�userExtension=1403�routing=branc".
000087     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000089     "h�routeLoc=K-MISS�routeAttn=Joe�comments=Comments ".
000090     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000092     "Go Here�debit�date=121306�amount=100.00�sequenceNb".
000093     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000095     "r=12345678��credit�date=051406�amount=900.00�seque".
000096     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000098     "nceNbr=11122233��ATM�date=010106�amount=123.45��ch".
000099     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000101     "argeback�date=010106�amount=500.00��statement�date".
000102     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000104     "=032906�amount=1000.00�                           ".
000105 01  INPUT-DATA REDEFINES IN-DATA PIC X(400).
000106
000112
000113 01  VARIOUS-COUNTS USAGE COMP.
000114     12 MAX-ARGUMENTS    PIC S9(4).
000115     12 INPUT-DATA-POS   PIC S9(4).
000116     12 STRING-PARM-LEN  PIC S9(4).
000117     12 J                PIC S9(4).
000119     12 INPUT-DATA-LENGTH PIC S9(4).
000120     12 NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS PIC S9(4).
000121
000122
000130 01  VARIOUS-OTHER-DATA.
000140     12 INPUT-STRING-ID     PIC X(25).
000150     12 INPUT-STRING-PARM   PIC X(25).
000151     12 NV-WORK             PIC X(60).
000152     12 MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER PIC X VALUE "�".
000153     12 MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR PIC X VALUE "=".
000154
000160 01  FLAGS.
000161     12 FINISH-FLAG         PIC X VALUE SPACE.
000162        88 FINISHED           VALUE '1'.
000163        88 NOT-FINISHED       VALUE '0'.
000164     12 REQUEST-FLAG        PIC X VALUE SPACE.
000165        88 END-OF-REQUEST           VALUE '1'.
000166        88 NOT-END-OF-REQUEST       VALUE '0'.
000167     12 NAME-VALUE-FLAG      PIC X VALUE SPACE.
000168        88 ITSA-NAME           VALUE '1'.
000169        88 ITSA-VALUE          VALUE '0'.
000170
000171
000172
000180 PROCEDURE DIVISION.
000190 MAIN SECTION.
000191 000.
000192     PERFORM 100-INITIAL-SETUP
000193     PERFORM 200-PROCESSING UNTIL FINISHED
000194*     PERFORM 900-CLOSE-DOWN
000195     STOP RUN
000196     .
000197*>===========================================================
000200 100-INITIAL-SETUP SECTION.
000201 110-IS.
000202     SET NOT-FINISHED TO TRUE
000210     PERFORM 2000-LOAD-ARGUMENTS
000220      *> IN THIS SCENARIO THE ARGUMENTS ARE PARSED AND LOADED
000221      *> ONCE
000230      *> DURING INITIALIZATION.
000231      *>
000232      *> IT IS A GENERAL PURPOSE LOAD ROUTINE. (WORKS FOR ANY
000233      *> PROGRAM WITH PARAMETERS IN THE NAME=VALUE FORMAT).
000234      *>
000240      *>
000250      *> ON COMPLETION ALL ARGUMENTS HAVE BEEN LOADED INTO THE
000260      *> "ARGUMENTS" ARRAY. GROUPS OF ARGUMENTS THAT REPRESENT
000261      *> A "RECORD" WILL HAVE THE GROUP FLAG SET IN THE LAST NAME
000262      *> /VALUE PAIR OF THE GROUP
000270      *>
000280      *> INPUT-STRING-ID AND INPUT-STRING-PARM CAN BE LOADED FROM
000281      *> THIS
000290      *> ARRAY USING THE ARGS-X1 INDEX. THIS IS DONE BY PERFORMING
000291      *> 2100-PARSE-INPUT-DATA.
000300      *>
000310     .
000311 199-IS.
000312     EXIT.
000313*>================================================================
000314
000320 200-PROCESSING SECTION.
000321 210-P.
000330     *> VARIOUS PROCESSING OCCURS HERE...
000340
000350     PERFORM 2100-PARSE-INPUT-DATA  *> GET THE NEXT NAME/VALUE
000351                                    *> PAIR
000360
000370     *> PROCESSING CONTINUES....USING INPUT-STRING-ID
000380     *>                           AND INPUT-STRING-PARM
000390     *> AS AT PRESENT.
000391
000400     SET FINISHED TO TRUE
000480     .
000490 299-P.
000500     EXIT.
000561*>==============================================================
000562*>
000563*>          SUBROUTINES ACTIVATED FROM ABOVE...
000564*>
000565*>==============================================================
000566 2000-LOAD-ARGUMENTS     SECTION.
000567 2000-LA-000.
000568     *> THE FOLLOWING CODE PARSES THE NAME/VALUE PAIRS IN
000569     *> INPUT-DATA
000570     *> AND LOADS THEM INTO THE ARGUMENTS ARRAY.
000571     *>
000572     MOVE SPACES TO ARGUMENTS
000573     IF INPUT-DATA (1:1) = MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
000574        MOVE 2 TO INPUT-DATA-POS   *> STEP OVER FIRST FIELD
000575                                   *> DELIMITER
000576                                   *> IF ONE IS PRESENT
000577     ELSE
000578        MOVE 1 TO INPUT-DATA-POS
000579     END-IF
000580     COMPUTE INPUT-DATA-LENGTH = FUNCTION STORED-CHAR-LENGTH
000581                                          (INPUT-DATA)
000582     *> IF YOUR ENVIRONMENT DOESN'T SUPPORT THE ABOVE
000583     *> INTRINSIC FUNCTION, YOU WILL NEED TO ESTABLISH
000584     *> THE TOTAL LENGTH OF THE PARAMETER STRINGS
000585     *> IN "INPUT-DATA" USING "INSPECT" OR ONE OF THE
000586     *> TECHNIQUES DISCUSSED IN CLC
000587     MOVE ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT TO MAX-ARGUMENTS
000588     SET ITSA-NAME TO TRUE
000589     SET ARGS-X1 TO 1
000590     MOVE 1 TO J   *> POINTER USED TO BUILD EACH NAME OR VALUE
000591     PERFORM
000592        VARYING INPUT-DATA-POS
000593           FROM INPUT-DATA-POS
000594             BY 1
000595        UNTIL INPUT-DATA-POS > INPUT-DATA-LENGTH OR
000596              ARGS-X1 > MAX-ARGUMENTS
000598                 EVALUATE  INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1)
000599                    WHEN  MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR
000600                       SET ITSA-VALUE TO TRUE
000601                       MOVE 1 TO J
000602                    WHEN  MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
000603                       SET ITSA-NAME TO TRUE
000604                       IF INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS + 1:1) = 
MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
000605                          SET ARG-END-OF-GROUP (ARGS-X1) TO TRUE
000607                       END-IF
000608                       MOVE 1 TO J
000609                       SET ARGS-X1 UP BY 1
000610                    WHEN OTHER
000611                       IF ITSA-NAME
000612                          MOVE INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) TO 
ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1) (J:1)
000613                          ADD 1 TO J
000614                       ELSE
000615                          MOVE INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) TO 
ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1) (J:1)
000616                          ADD 1 TO J
000617                       END-IF
000618                  END-EVALUATE
000650     END-PERFORM
000651     SET NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS TO ARGS-X1
000652     SUBTRACT 1 FROM NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS
000653     SET ARGS-X1 TO 1 *> SET INDEX FOR USE FROM MAINLINE CODE
000654     SET ARGS-X1 DOWN BY 1
000655     .
000656 2000-LA-999.
000657     EXIT.
000658 *>==============================================================
000659 2100-PARSE-INPUT-DATA     SECTION.
000660 2100-PID-000.
000661 *> THIS CODE LOADS INPUT-STRING-ID AND INPUT-STRING-PARM WITH
000662 *> THE NEXT
000663 *> VALID NAME/VALUE PAIR.
000664 *> IT DOESN'T PARSE THE INPUT-DATA BUT THE EFFECT IS THE SAME AS
000665 *> IF IT HAD...
000666     SET ARGS-X1 UP BY 1
000667     IF  ARGS-X1 NOT > NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS
000668         MOVE ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1) TO INPUT-STRING-ID
000669         MOVE ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1) TO INPUT-STRING-PARM
000670         IF ARG-END-OF-GROUP (ARGS-X1)
000671            SET END-OF-REQUEST TO TRUE
000672         ELSE
000673            SET NOT-END-OF-REQUEST TO TRUE
000674         END-IF
000675     ELSE
000676       MOVE SPACE TO INPUT-STRING-ID
000677                     INPUT-STRING-PARM
000678     END-IF
000679     .
000680 2100-PID-999.
000681     EXIT.
000682*>============================ END OF PROGRAM ===================
000870


A few comments about the above...

1. The test for a delimiter at the start could be removed if it is 
absolutely certain that no such delimiter will ever be encountered.
2. If a double delimiter is encountered INPUT-DATA-POS could be incremented 
by 1 to step over it (for  a marginal efficiency gain), but the logic works 
whether you do this or not.
3. The last group of parms will not set the group flag unless they are 
delimited by a double delimiter. It is very easy to change this so that the 
last group is always set as a group by adding 1 line to the code. (Or 
ensuring input is terminated by a double delimiter...)
4. Because of the proportional font used in these messages, the code looks 
pretty awful when posted here. In a proper Editor, properly formatted as 
COBOL source, it looks much better. :-)

This code does exactly what is required with no work areas, no UNSTRINGs, a 
single pass parse of the input data, and also stores the whole parameter set 
as a single, one-time task during initialization. (there are a number of 
advantages in doing this).

HOWEVER, the code requires the input to be in the expected format. It 
doesn't deal with embedded spaces or syntax errors. If I were designing 
this, I would make the parameters free format and remove the delimiter. 
Parameters would ALWAYS be name/value pairs separated by a single equals 
sign. (If you really just want a parm with no value, set the value to 
"dummy" or "present" or some agreed string.) Doing this means the parms can 
be easily entered from a variety of inputs, and they can be checked for 
validity and syntax before having their values validated.

<snip>>
> The thing I like about my original method, other than requiring two
> unstrings, is that no temporary field is required.
>

Don't like work fields? See above... :-)


> Anyway, thanks for giving it a shot!
>

It really was a pleasure, Frank. I'm not saying it is the best solution, but 
it's the best I can do in the time I allotted for this. Hopefully, some 
people will get a few ideas from it... :-)

COBOL is definitely fun to write and I'll miss that aspect of it. Maybe, in 
time, I'll get to feel the same about C#... I like it, it is simple and 
concise, but I'm not facile enough with it yet to really push the envelope. 
I had a major breakthrough with it yesterday when I managed to get it to 
raise an event (when the event hadn't actually occurred) and so save 
duplicating all the code that handled that event... :-) It was quite 
bizarre.. I waded through pages of example code, read a whole lot of stuff 
about raising various kinds of events (none of which were what I actually 
wanted), traced through some very advanced delegation classes until my head 
swum, then a light flashed on ... "Why don't I just..." did it and 
everything worked... with one line of code...:-)

Pete.
```

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>

would ever have any, but just in case.  We could, of course, wrap strings
inside of quotes, but we felt this was simpler.  The request is always
generated by a program, so I'm not too worried about how simple it is for a

Many people would share it. However, I believe that because it is less than 
a dozen lines of code and provided it is commented, most people would see 
what the code is trying to do.

The EVALUATE makes it very clear that if a delimiter is encountered the next 
thing will be a parameter Name and if an = is encountered, what follows will 
be a Value. (If no value is present the delimiter forces a reset back to the 
name). Having the specific relationship between these things automatically 
documented by EVALUATE, I think, is a bonus.

The only "hairy" bit I can see are the two subscripted refmodded lines used 
to build the name and values into the master ARGUMENTS table. Arnold 
commented on this, but agreed he understood how they worked.

Obviously, I think it is OK :-)

>
>>HOWEVER, the code requires the input to be in the expected format. It
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> inside of quotes, but we felt this was simpler.

I noted that "this is a comment" had embedded spaces so perhaps the 
delimiters are useful after all... :-)

I see no difference (apart from the character chosen) between having a ' or 
having a |... Are they not logically equivalent in this case?


>The request is always
> generated by a program, so I'm not too worried about how simple it is for 
> a
> user to enter it.
>

Fair enough. Then they can be fixed format...

>>> Anyway, thanks for giving it a shot!

…[25 more quoted lines elided]…

add rams to ewes giving lambs.

OR

01 penis size is enormous class is alpha
              usage is internal floating-point.

(Sadly no longer valid, but worked in COBOL 59, so long as 'enormous' was a 
comp item, separately defined, with a value of  4 or 8)


OR

alter points to proceed to head-on-train-wreck

OR

read newspaper, at end set fire to it.

There are some others I can think of but probably not suitable for family 
viewing and, strictly speaking SQL, not COBOL... :-)

…[5 more quoted lines elided]…

<SNIP>

>>I noted that "this is a comment" had embedded spaces so perhaps the
>>delimiters are useful after all... :-)
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Ah. I was thinking...

'function=do this'     'name=Frank Swarbrick'

Here's the amended COBOL to do your interpretation...

                EVALUATE  INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1)
                       WHEN  MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR
000600                       SET ITSA-VALUE TO TRUE
000601                       MOVE 1 TO J

000602           WHEN  MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
000603                   IF INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS + 1:1) = SPACE
                                    SET ITSA-NAME TO TRUE
                                    MOVE 1 TO J
                                    SET ARGS-X1 UP BY 1
                              END-IF
                              IF INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS + 1:1) = 
MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
000605                          SET ARG-END-OF-GROUP (ARGS-X1) TO TRUE
000607                  END-IF
000608
000609
000610           WHEN OTHER
000611                   IF ITSA-NAME
                                    IF INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) NOT = 
SPACE
000612                             MOVE INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) TO 
ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1) (J:1)
000613                             ADD 1 TO J
                                    END-IF
000614                   ELSE
000615                          MOVE INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) TO 
ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1) (J:1)
000616                          ADD 1 TO J
000617                   END-IF
000618    END-EVALUATE

It took 5 minutes to do this, but I haven't tested it.

NOTE:
1. MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER now has a value of  ' (single quote)
2. Name/value pairs are now free format and can be separated by any number 
of
    spaces (there must be at least 1...).
2. Values cannot start with a space, but may contain embedded spaces...
     name='Frank Swarbrick'  is OK... comment=' some comment here' is NOT OK
     (It would require one more line to make this so that a leading space is 
OK, but then
      name/value pairs would always require at least two spaces separating 
them.)
3. END-OF-GROUP is now detected by two single quotes...''
4. Name/value pairs must have at least one space separating them.

The point about this is that it is pretty easy to amend, but any change in 
the syntax will result in a corresponding change in the 'rules'.

<snip>

>>> To be honest, I often find COBOL the opposite of fun to write, because
> its
…[29 more quoted lines elided]…
> consider COBOL to be one of them.  :-)

Not at all, but I do think (as Mary Poppins observed) a spoonful of sugar 
helps the medicine go down...:-)

>
>>> Just last night I was
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
> experience with C#, so I doubt I'd have an answer.

I find that the Help is excellent and the examples very good, but I'm still 
reserving the right to join the community forum...:-) If I get really stuck

> I got my COBOL delegate stuff working last night.  Had three delegates
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> I will post my code this weekend, if I remember.

Do try. I'd be interested to see it.

Pete.

	MOVE SPACE TO MUST-BE-SPACE MUST-NOT-BE-SPACE.
	UNSTRING INPUT-FIELD DELIMITED BY ALL SPACE
		INTO MUST-NOT-BE-SPACE MUST-BE-SPACE.
	IF MUST-BE-SPACE IS NOT EQUAL TO SPACE
		OR
	   MUST-NOT-BE-SPACE IS EQUAL TO SPACE
		DISPLAY "Danger Will Robinson !"
		DISPLAY "Input must contain data with"
		DISPLAY "no embedded spaces!".


Younger folk may not recognized the reference.

Donald
```

```

"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> schrieb im Newsbeitrag 
news:500b4bF1d47t2U1@mid.individual.net...

> 000057 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
> 000058 01  ARGUMENTS.
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> 000070*> MUST MATCH VALUE IN OCCURS ABOVE.

This previous comment highlights a problem, that we also encounter 
sometimes: how can we enforce, that the same value/literal is used in 
various places within a program? Assuming that a COBOL compiler supporting 
the REPLACE statement is available, we found a solution, that could be 
applied to the example above like this:

     REPLACE  ==a-t-l== BY ==40==.
     ....
     ....
         12 NAME-VALUE-PAIR OCCURS a-t-l
     ....
     01  ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT  PIC S9(4) COMP VALUE a-t-l.
     ....

Are there any experiences with such an approach?
Any pro and con arguments would be welcome.

Karl Kiesel
Fujitsu Siemens Computers, M�nchen

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Productivity

_(reply depth: 17)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2007-01-06T00:43:21+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<506ruoF1ehb1uU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4v33ipF1a006cU1@mid.individual.net> <12oosqtmgaqcd81@news.supernews.com> <4v7ajgF1bf6u8U1@mid.individual.net> <1166980834.471149.102990@i12g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <4v8qu1F1b75r0U1@mid.individual.net> <dElkh.4094$yx6.3439@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net> <4vf0t1F1bfj5nU1@mid.individual.net> <4vfl66F1as7a4U1@mid.individual.net> <4vgj6mF1a4g7nU1@mid.individual.net> <4vimr5F1cedo7U1@mid.individual.net> <4vj2kkF1co1akU1@mid.individual.net> <4vlbkiF1bf56sU1@mid.individual.net> <4vlnqgF1c247oU1@mid.individual.net> <4vm6ldF16ggd7U1@mid.individual.net> <4vvj6rF1dqm00U1@mid.individual.net> <500b4bF1d47t2U1@mid.individual.net> <enl1cs$4lg$1@nntp.fujitsu-siemens.com>`

```

"Karl Kiesel" <Karl.Kiesel@fujitsu-siemens.com> wrote in message 
news:enl1cs$4lg$1@nntp.fujitsu-siemens.com...
>
> "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> schrieb im 
…[30 more quoted lines elided]…
>
This is the most imaginative use of COPY I have ever seen :-)

Full marks for imagination and thinking "outside the square".

I've never seen this before and I am blown away by the idea of it.

However, I probably won't use it :-).

These are all personal opinions and there is no reason why people (who don't 
have my prejudices) shouldn't use this approach. Here's why I personally 
will not adopt it:

1. I HATE using COBOL COPY. If it is source code for a frequently used 
routine, I  simply write a subprogram (or subClass). If it is source for a 
file definition or working-storage record layout, I don't use the COBOL file 
system so I don't need them. (I have been known to create a COPY block for 
SQL Host variables, but this does not require REPLACING, as the names are 
DECLGENed and only used in one place in the program. (Within an SQL DECLARE 
block...) It requires a DECLGEN if the database changes, and then the 
DECLGEN has to be applied to the COPY block, and all the programs that use 
the COPY block must be recompiled... too much like hard work.)  Eventually I 
realised that a separation layer made the whole thing much simpler and that 
is what I use currently. My application programs don't contain ESQL any 
more. They call an interface. As I move off COBOL this becomes even simpler 
with immediate result sets returned and manipulated offline. I'm liking this 
approach more and more. Things like Data Adapters, Table Adapters and 
Readers in C# make ESQL look Stone Age. Why open a cursor and maintain a DB 
connection so you can run it, when you can run it offline...? Sure, the 
programs require SQL strings to tell them what to get, but they don't need 
to hold a DB Connection once they have got it.

(If you are working in an environment where they use high-powered tools like 
ENDEVOR, which are designed specifically for source management, it isn't so 
bad, but if you have to manage it yourself it becomes a nightmare. Never 
mind source code management, I had to write my own DECLGEN for the PC, 
because there isn't one in the environment I work with. I'm not planning on 
writing ENDEVOR any time soon... :-))

2. I don't need or want to maintain COBOL source,  and using COPY just 
perpetuates this.

3. I can see the above solution becoming confusing if there are a number of 
variables being maintained by it, but I expect this could be managed by 
using suitable COPY Names.

4. If the variable is maintained within the program, close to whatever it 
applies to, it is easy for a Programmer to check the value. If an external 
source has to be updated in isolation, I see this as a potential source of 
error ( for example, using the example cited...Two things are being updated 
in two places; the OCCURS value on the table, and a separate field that 
reflects the limit on the array. Using the proposed approach these two 
things must be updated in two separate places (The OCCURS in the source 
program and the limit in the COPY book.) Provided changes are only made 
rarely it is a good way to ensure the value of the limit variable, but so is 
coding it as a VALUE within the program... :-) Bottom line: For this type of 
instance, it probably isn't much help.

Having said all of that, I can see cases where the suggested approach WOULD 
be very viable. For independent variables in WS, where the said variable is 
defined in many programs, this would be a very good way to administer the 
value of the variable from a single central point.

Thanks, Karl, for a really imaginative and thought-provoking use of 
COPY...REPLACING.

Pete.

Pete





> Are there any experiences with such an approach?
> Any pro and con arguments would be welcome.
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

```
Pete Dashwood<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> 01/05/07 4:43 AM >>>
>
>1. I HATE using COBOL COPY. If it is source code for a frequently used 
>routine, I  simply write a subprogram (or subClass). If it is source for a

>file definition or working-storage record layout, I don't use the COBOL
file 
>system so I don't need them. (I have been known to create a COPY block for

>SQL Host variables, but this does not require REPLACING, as the names are 
>DECLGENed and only used in one place in the program. (Within an SQL DECLARE

>block...) It requires a DECLGEN if the database changes, and then the 
>DECLGEN has to be applied to the COPY block, and all the programs that use

>the COPY block must be recompiled... too much like hard work.)  Eventually
I 
>realised that a separation layer made the whole thing much simpler and that

>is what I use currently. My application programs don't contain ESQL any 
>more. They call an interface. As I move off COBOL this becomes even simpler

>with immediate result sets returned and manipulated offline. I'm liking
this 
>approach more and more. Things like Data Adapters, Table Adapters and 
>Readers in C# make ESQL look Stone Age. Why open a cursor and maintain a DB

>connection so you can run it, when you can run it offline...? Sure, the 
>programs require SQL strings to tell them what to get, but they don't need

>to hold a DB Connection once they have got it.

A few comments...

One, how do you keep your linkage areas in sync without using copybooks? 
Take the following production code:

     MOVE GENERIC-ACCT-SUBR      TO SUBROUTINE         
     CALL SUBROUTINE USING       GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT    
                                 GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT   
                                 GENERIC-ACCT-ERROR    
                                 PSB-PCB-INFO          
                                 ADDRESS OF PCB-PTR-TBL
     ON EXCEPTION                                      
         GO TO 9850-COBOL-ERROR                        
     END-CALL                                          

GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT is defined in a copybook called "GENACCTI".
GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT is defined in a copybook called "GENACCTO".
etc.

GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT has twelve distinict input fields.  GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT
has over thirty output (result) fields.  This would be a nightmare without
the copybooks.

Question about your comment about 'intermediate result sets' being
manipulated offline...  This sounds good in theory, and I'm sure it works
most of the time, but I imagine it would not be a good thing if your select
returned hundreds of thousands of rows.  Would you agree?  I guess I'm still
thinking in my "batch processing" mindset, so perhaps that's something you
would simply never need to do.

Frank




--- 
Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA
```

```

"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in message 
news:507nhmF1f24rfU1@mid.individual.net...
> Pete Dashwood<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> 01/05/07 4:43 AM >>>
>>
…[55 more quoted lines elided]…
> the copybooks.

Sure. But I wouldn't be calling SUBROUTINE with parameters.

It would be a Class and GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT would be a set of properties, as 
would GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT. There is then no requirement for the linkage to 
be "in sync", because there is no linkage.

You could still use COPY to define these areas in the calling program if you 
wanted to, but the object properties would simply be an interface block 
large enough to accommodate both of GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT and 
GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT (plus the other two parameters you pass currently. (I'd 
put these at the "top" of the interface block, along with a return code and 
error message. Fixed fields that will not change...)).
...
invoke
   objSubroutine "SET-interface"
         using interface-block
end-invoke
invoke
     objSubroutine "AnyMethod" *> method to manipulate properties as 
currently defined
end-invoke
invoke objSubroutine "GET-interface-block"
     returning interface-block
end-invoke
...

Now a new-field gets added to GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT and a couple of new fields 
are added to GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT...

You could override the existing Method or extend it to a new method or use a 
different interface, there are a number of options.

You'd probably take this decision based on how many existing programs are 
affected by the changes.

If they all are, then the Class could be amended to reflect the new 
interface (although I prefer not to do this, personally...)

Now your amendments in the application programs focus on how the new fields 
get used; the code to invoke Subroutine doesn't change, and there is no 
requirement for parameter lists or linkage syncing.

If only some of the apps are affected by the new fields, I'd  probably add a 
new method (maybe inheriting from/ extending the old one...) that recognises 
the interface change.

All of the programs that DON'T use the new stuff will function as they 
always have, without change. I don't believe they require regression 
testing, but it is arguable, depending on the circumstances and the 
interactions between the apps. (If COPY Books are used, everything requires 
regression testing because even programs that don't use the new fields have 
had their interface changed).

I am trying to demonstrate a concept here, it is not a perfect example.

Conceptually, a called subroutine with a parameter list is like a Class with 
a single static interface. The OO approach allows a separation between the 
behaviours (Methods) and the interfaces to them, which cannot be easily 
achieved with procedural programming.

>
> Question about your comment about 'intermediate result sets' being
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> returned hundreds of thousands of rows.  Would you agree?

I'm not sure. It really depends on the environment you are working in, I 
think.

>I guess I'm still
> thinking in my "batch processing" mindset, so perhaps that's something you
> would simply never need to do.

Certainly, the transactional approach would reduce the size of result 
sets... :-)

Pete.
```
